;五月。@
;桜の散った日も今や遠く、夏の日差しも遠い、曖昧な季節。¥
`May.@
br
`The days marked by scattered cherry blossoms were long past.  The days scorched by the blazing summer sun were yet to come.  May was in between.  May was uncertain of itself.  May was ambiguous and beguiling.¥

;柔らかな日差しは、
;眠気を誘うような温もりを与え続けている。¥
`The gentle sunlight whispered its warmth onto my skin, soothing and inviting like a lullaby.¥

;辺りの空気には少々の湿気も感じ始め、
;梅雨が少しずつ近づいていた。¥
`The air was beginning to take on the faintest hint of moisture.  The rainy season was close by, waiting.¥

delay 1000

;五月。@
;始まりの季節から、少しだけ走った後の季節。¥
`May.@
br
`A month that arrives -- whether you want it to or not -- just by walking a few blocks from the beginning.¥

;新しい環境に慣れ始め、
;辺りのことが少しだけ広く見え始める頃。¥
`A month where everything's still new, everything's still settling in.  A month that only wishes it knew what's in store.@
br
`A month that sees the rest of the year spread out before its very eyes -- for better or for worse.¥

;始まってから少し。終わるまでは遠い、曖昧な期間。¥

;五月一日。日曜日。午後４時半。@
;マンションの５階にある自分の六畳一間の部屋には、
;夕焼けの光が差し込んでいた。¥
`May first.  Sunday.  4:00 PM.@
br
`My nine-by-twelve single was on the fifth floor of an apartment complex.@
br
`The fiery lights of sunset were shining into my room.¥

;部屋の壁にはスーツとＹシャツが
;ハンガーに掛けられている。@
;小さめな冷蔵庫や炊飯器。電子レンジなども、
;狭い六畳の部屋に並んでいる。¥
`Suits and shirts were hung up on the walls.@
br
`Other things lined up in my shoebox apartment were a tiny fridge, a rice cooker, a microwave oven, and what have you.¥

;つまる所、
;”一人暮らしの社会人の部屋”という物そのままだった。¥
`The very picture of a "bachelor pad for a young cubicle rat".¥

;そんな部屋の隅っこで、椅子にだらしなく
;全身を持たれかけて座っているのが俺だったりする。¥
`I found myself flopped in a chair, arms wrapped around myself, in a corner of the room.  NO FREAKING CLUE why.¥

;溝口春樹（みぞぐちはるき）、２２歳。いわゆる新入社員。
;今年度から社会人になりました。
;…なってしまいました。¥
`My name is Haruki Mizoguchi.  I'm 22 years old.  I'm fresh meat at a corporation.  That's right, I became a card-punching corporate monkey just this year ... not exactly of my own free will or anything.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「…あ〜、暇…」¥
`"... man ... I'm bored ..."¥

;一人暮らしを始めて一ヶ月。
;いつの間にか独り言が多くなっていた。¥
`It was, what, a month since I started living by myself.  Somewhere in there I started talking to myself.  A lot.¥

;この行動に深い意味は無い。
;別段、寂しさといったセンチメンタルな理由ではない。¥
`I don't really think that fact had any deep or special meaning, by the way.  And don't you dare get all sentimental on me and go "awww, he's so lonely", either.  Because I wasn't.¥

;部屋に帰った後に『ただいま』と言う習慣をつけていた所、
;いつの間にか癖になっていただけだったりする。¥
`It was just things like how I still said "I'm home" when I opened the door. Sometime or other, I'd gotten in the habit.  Weird, isn't it?¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「…別段、やることもないしなぁ…」¥
`"... man, there's nothing I want to do ..."¥

;横に視線をずらせばテレビゲームの筐体。@
;専ら、学生の時の休日はコイツと遊んでいたものの、
;こっちに来てからは電源を入れる回数が
;めっきり少なくなっていた。¥
`I looked around and noticed my video game console.@
br
`Way back when I was a student, this was it.  This was what I did on vacation.  But I'd hardly even flipped the switch on this thing since I moved it here.¥

;すっかりと熱が冷め切ってしまい、
;今や無用の長物になってしまっている。¥
`So the circuits went from nearly burning out, to cold and neglected.  And so now what had been my most prized possession was a useless heap of silicon and plastic.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「…外行って、金使うのも何だしなぁ…」¥
`"But if I go out, I'm gonna end up wasting money ..."¥

;会社に勤めるようになって一ヶ月経つが、
;実は未だに給料を貰っていなかったりする。¥
`Even though I'd been working at the company for a month, they hadn't actually cut me a paycheck yet.¥

;その訳は、４月の分を５月末に貰う…という
;至って普通な理由だったりする。¥
`All companies did this sort of thing.  I'd get April's pay in my May salary.¥

;引越しの時点で親から支援金をたっぷりと頂いていたが、
;必要な物を揃えたりしていたら相当削れてしまっていた。¥
`When I moved out, my parents had been pretty generous.  Still, I was trying to keep expenses down to a minimum.¥

;さすがに、毎日パンの耳で過ごす生活には遠いものの、
;贅沢が出来る財政でも無かった。¥
`Of course, it's not like I was living on bread and water, but I had no disposable income to speak of.¥

; `[ 溝口 春樹 ]
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「…………」¥
`"... ... ..."¥

;絶妙な行動の板バサミの中、ぼんやりと天井を見つめる。¥
`What an amazing place to find myself stuck in -- that's right, between a rock and a hard place.  I stared at the ceiling without really seeing it.¥

;夕日に照らされ、淡い褐色を帯びた部屋。
;外からのかすかな音と時計の秒針音だけが響いている。¥
`The sunset filtered in, painting my room a pale sepia.  The only sounds audible in my room were faint voices from outside, and the tick-tock of my watch.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
;「”時間があったら、何かしなくちゃいけない”
;  って思うのは、日本人の悪い癖って言ってたよなぁ…」¥
`"Idle hands are the Devil's playthings."  The tenet by which all of Japan ran, apparently.  And I HATED it ...¥

;学生の頃の旅行で聞いた言葉は、
;誰に届くわけでもなく部屋に漂っていた。¥
`It was the sort of thing I'd get told on field trips as a student.  There were no chaperones to harass me now, but I could hear those words haunting my room.¥

;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
bg black,3
;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
delay 500

;結局。¥
`So.  In the end.¥

;五分ぐらい経った後に、
;冷蔵庫の中が寂しくなっていることを思い出し、
;外に出ることにする。¥
`After I bummed around for five minutes or so, I decided that the interior of my fridge was looking REALLY empty and lonely, and ended up going outside after all.¥

;何も落ち込む要素もないのに、深いため息をついていた。¥
`I left the room, shut and locked the door.@
br
`I wasn't depressed, nothing like that, really.  But I let out a deep sigh anyway.¥

;五階から見える街の景色は少々寂しげに見える。¥
`Five floors up from the street, I could see the town yawning in the evening light.@
br
`It was a lonely feeling.¥

;マンション内に響いていた。¥
`I walked stiffly down the stairwell.  The echoes of my steps were the only sounds in the complex.¥

*Gogatsu_1_1b

;マンションを出ると、強く柔らかい風が体に当たってくる。@
;茜色に染まる空。情緒の理解のない俺でも
;『綺麗だなぁ』程度は思える。¥
`The instant I stepped outside, I was greeted by a strong, yet tender, breeze.¥
`The sky was red all over, like it had been dipped in a scarlet dye.  It was a sight for sore eyes -- so striking that even someone as oblivious as me could say that it was absolutely beautiful.¥

;駅へと続く道沿いには、日曜なのに仕事帰りの
;サラリーマンや地元の主婦などがちらほらと見えた。¥
`Here and there, all along the path to the train station, I saw salarymen returning from work (on a Sunday!), and housewives who lived around here.¥

;そんな、よくある光景に溶け込むように、
;近くのスーパーまでの道のりを歩き出す。¥
`Nothing out of the ordinary.  I slipped right into the scene.  Dissolved into the crowd of people.  Started to walk towards a nearby supermarket.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「（今日は何を作ろうか…？
;　そーいや、鶏肉が少し残ってたっけか…）」¥
`"(What am I going to make today?  Well, I think I might have a bit of chicken left ...)"¥

;頭の中で、”本日の献立”と、
;”今週一週間の献立”を考えながら歩いていく。@
`And so I walked along, thinking about what was on the menu for today and planning out my meals for the rest of the week.¥

;こんな構想も、引越ししたての頃は新鮮だったものの、
;一ヶ月も過ぎれば日課に過ぎなくなってしまっていた。¥
`I hadn't ever dealt with these considerations before the move.  But after a month of living alone, it became just another part of the daily grind.¥

delay 500

;申し訳程度の街路樹は、
;五月らしい新緑の緑を風に揺らしていた。
;夕日の赤が混じり、独特の色を映している。¥
`Frail little trees alongside the road were fresh as May itself, wearing their young green finery and swaying in the wind.  Their colors flared against the red sunset, causing the air to echo with so many hues new to this world.¥

;夕暮れ時にも、うららかな陽気は辺りを包んでいる。
;何かの花の匂いを僅かに感じ、春であることを感じていた。¥
`It was dusk, but I was getting this cheerful, lighthearted vibe.  I could just barely smell the perfume of flowers on the air -- announcing to me and the world that spring had come.¥

br

;きっと、理由なんて程の物は無かった。¥
`I'm pretty sure there was no rhyme or reason to what I did next:¥

;足を止め、耳を澄まし、音源と思われる方向に
;足先を向けたことに、深い理由は無かった。¥
`I stopped walking, focused on the music, and figured out where it was coming from.  Then I started for that general direction.  Like I said, the reason was not what you'd call a "profound" one.¥

;ただ単に、『他にやることもないし』というだけの、
;自分でも情けないくらいの
;ネガティブな感情による行動だった。¥
`I had absolutely nothing else to do.  That was all the reason I had, born of an apathy so malignant that even *I* could see how pathetic I was.¥

;ピアノの音に誘われて…
;というフレーズを自分に投影させて、
;詩人ぶりたかったのかもしれない。¥
`I indulged in a little narrative of my life.  "Enticed by the piano's song, our intrepid hero ..."  Uh huh.  Ladies and gentlemen, the next Poet Laureate of Japan.¥

delay 1500

;理由は何であれ、
;進む足はピアノの音へ向けて進んでいった。¥
`Anyway.  For whatever reason, my feet were moving.  Moving towards the music. ¥

;ただそれだけのことで、
;これからの日々が少しだけ変わることなど、
;一片も思わぬままに。¥
`And it never even crossed my mind that this random little act might have any lasting impact on my life.¥

delay 500

;風が吹いて、新緑の木々が揺れて、
;少しだけピアノの音が薄れた。¥
`A gust of wind rustled through the branches and the leaves.  The piano music continued past the white noise, a little weakened.¥

;耳を澄まして、見えない糸を手繰るように、
;夕暮れの街路を歩いていく。¥
`I walked along that sunset road, ears straining to hear and follow the thread of the melody, the way a drowning man grasped at a lifeline he couldn't even see.¥

delay 500

*Gogatsu_1_1c

;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
bg "May/BackGround/Kamiake_Gaikan_red.jpg",3
;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>

;しばらく歩いて、目の前に現れたのは一軒の神社だった。¥
`After I'd walked a while, I found myself looking at a Shinto temple.¥

;マンション等の集合住宅の立ち並ぶ中に、
;ぽっかりと空いた穴のような場所。¥
`There was a row of apartment buildings pressing against each other and themselves.  And then there was this temple.  Its open spaces almost seemed like a vacuum in comparison.¥

;あまり古さを感じない小奇麗な拝殿が小さく建ち、
;その周りには大きな木が一本。¥
`It was a small, beautifully kept structure.  Didn't look as old as I might've expected a temple to be.  In its courtyard grew a single, large tree.¥

;その周囲に薄く展開するゴミ一つ無い綺麗な地面には、
;自転車の轍が薄く見える。¥
`On the undeveloped, unlittered, completely pristine landscape, I saw the faint tread marks of a bicycle.¥

;目を凝らすと、棒か何かで地面に線を引いた跡も見えた。
;きっと、近所の子供の遊び場にもなっているのだろう。¥
`Upon closer examination, I could see lines in the dirt.  Clearly, they were made by young hands -- using sticks and branches in their play.  That had to be it; children used this place as their playground.¥

;その他には、水の流れていない手水舎が
;小さく置いてある程度。¥
`There was also one of those ritual stone basins you were supposed to wash your hands in before you could properly visit a shrine.  But the water wasn't running.  The setup seemed kind of neglected.¥

;街の中の小さな神社。
;ピアノの音は、明らかにその拝殿の中から流れていた。¥
`This was weird.  So not only was there this little temple here in this crowded area of town ...@
br
`... the stream of music was definitely coming from within.  Man, this was enough to make you do a double-take.¥

;やさしい音色はさながらＢＧＭのようで、
;その場がドラマのワンシーンを
;切り取ったような感触すら覚えた。¥
`The music was warm and moving, suffusing the entire area, making it all seem like the ending montage to a touching TV drama.¥

;ピアノと神社。
;考えてみればかなりのミスマッチな気がするが、
;案外合うものなのかもしれない。¥
`The problem was ...@
br
`... piano music and Shinto shrines didn't go together, not in my mind.  But hell, what did I know?¥

;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
bg "May/BackGround/Kamiake_Sekkin_red.jpg",3
;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>

;未だピアノの流れる社殿へ近づく。
;細かい砂利を踏む音がやけに騒がしく感じた。¥
`I was still approaching the shrine, and the music within.  I went closer, and closer.  Each step made a grinding noise on the fine sand of the courtyard.  My steps seemed so loud, and I felt like I was violating the grounds or something.¥

;五月十四日、金曜日。午後９時半。¥
`May fourteenth.  Friday.  9:30 PM.¥

;駅の中にある小さなチェーンの喫茶店には、
;名も知らぬジャズの曲と店員の張り上げた声、
;そして鈍く重い電車の音が響いていた。¥
`I was in this tiny coffee shop at the train station.  Staff were shouting, and some generic jazz tune was playing.  The dull, heavy sounds of a train on the tracks thundered over everything.¥

;未だに慣れないスーツにこぼさぬように、
;コーヒーカップに口をつける。酸味の強いコーヒーだなと、
;コーヒー通でもないのに批評を思う。¥
`I carefully raised the coffee cup to my lips, making sure I didn't spill anything on my suit.  The coffee was bitter, making me think snooty thoughts for a second about mouth feel and aftertaste.  But I was no coffee connoisseur, and neither was I used to wearing a suit.¥

;研修に疲れた頭が、コーヒーのカフェインで
;少しだけ明瞭になったような感覚を感じる。¥
`My head was heavy and listless with the weight of so much training, but the coffee seemed to help a little.¥

;【神明 みのり】
;「どうでもいいよ、そんなこと」¥
`[ Minori Kamiake ]
`"So what?  Why should I care?"¥

;みのりの一言に、
;俺はビルを破壊する時の巨大鉄球を連想した。¥
`Her statement made me imagine a wrecking ball, going through entire buildings without so much as a pause.¥

;容赦とか、
;そういうレベルを逸脱した攻撃力がそこにあった。¥
`I mean, there was so much offensive energy in it -- and absolutely ZERO mercy.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
;「…みのり、お前って何ていうか…すごいな」¥
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
`"Um ... you know, Minori ... how should I put this ... you're unbelievable."¥

;【神明 みのり】
;「それ絶対…褒めてないよね？」¥
`[ Minori Kamiake ]
`"Let me guess: those absolutely AREN'T words of praise."¥

;もはや何度目かも曖昧な、夕暮れ時の神明神社。
;ピアノを聴いた後。¥
`I'd almost lost count of how many times I'd come here to the Kamiake Shrine.  It was evening now, and the piano performance for the day was over.¥

;昨日の出来事を話していた所、俺はみのりに少しだけ
;今の悩みを打ち明けることになってしまっていた。¥
`I'd started talking to Minori about what had happened yesterday, hoping she'd understand a little bit of what I was going through.¥

;いわゆる、将来へ対する不安について。¥
`Hoping she'd understand how uncertain I found my own future these days.¥

;…結果は先程の通りだった。見事すぎる一蹴である。¥
`But as you can see, this operation ended in total failure.  She rejected every single thing I said.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
;「普通なら、
;　もう少し気の利いた言葉の一つや二つ出るもんだろ？」¥
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
`"I mean -- come on.  Aren't you usually supposed to say a sympathetic thing or two?  Isn't that what most people do?"¥

;【神明 みのり】
;「私、嘘を言うのは嫌いなんだよ」¥
`[ Minori Kamiake ]
`"I'm not your 'most people'.  Unlike them, I don't like lying."¥

;みのりは大真面目な顔で、
;それなりに酷い言葉を俺に投げかけている。¥
`She looked dead serious when she said spat these incredibly cruel words at me.¥

;思わず溜息が漏れ、
;その様を見たみのりは小さく『ドンマイ』と呟いた。¥
`I sighed, without intending to.  Minori noticed, and muttered "you're welcome".¥

;『本当にそう思っているのか』と聞いてみれば、
;みのりはやや苦笑い気味に再度『ドンマイ』と呟いた。¥
`And when I asked her "is that what you really think?" she repeated herself, this time with a bitter smile: "you're welcome".¥

;どうやら、昨日の同期の退職がトリガーとなったらしい。¥
`When that guy quit, it triggered something in me, as well.¥

;漠然としていた五月病がやや形を帯び、
;具体的な不安感へと出来上がっていた。¥
`The freshman blues I'd carried around with me like some vague weight on me now started to coalesce -- into a mass of suffocating anxiety.¥

;新しい世界へと踏み出した際の沢山の違和感が
;こうして形になっているのだろう。¥
`All the doubts and questions I'd had about stepping into the brave new world of adulthood were now being given shape.  I didn't like the shape they formed.¥

;目の前に迫っているわけでもない事なのに強い不安を感じ、
;昨日今日と陰鬱な気分が続いていた。¥
`I couldn't point to a single thing that I was facing and say, "this is what's bothering me".  And yet, in spite of that, yesterday's restless, unsettled feeling was turning me inside out.¥

;六畳一間の部屋は、
;生活するにはそれなりに役に立っているが、
;不安を解消するような機能は無く。¥
`And while my little shoebox of an apartment was certainly a necessity in that thing I called my life, it didn't have any place where I could drop off these feelings, make them go away.¥

;朝食を適当に作り、掃除を終え、
;必要になった雑貨を買いに行った後。
;相変わらず、足が神社へと向いていた。¥
`I threw together breakfast, cleaned up, and shopped for necessities.  And then, of course, I set off for the Kamiake Shrine as usual.¥

;決して、みのりに会いに行くのではなく、
;神社という憩いの場所へ行くためなのだと、
;どこかで何度も自分に言い聞かせながら。¥
`Telling myself the entire while that oh, it had nothing to do with seeing Minori -- I just wanted to go there for some rest and relaxation.¥

;神社に行けば
;みのりがいることなどは分かっているだろうに、
;いないことを僅かに祈っていた。¥
`And I hoped -- a little bit -- that Minori wouldn't be there, even though I knew that chances were she'd be there all right.¥

;そして。¥
`In the end ...¥

;神社に着き、みのりの姿を確認して、
;少しだけ喜んでいた自分に情けなさと敗北感を感じた。¥
`... when I drew near to the shrine and saw Minori standing there, the tiny amount of hope I'd had vanished, only to be replaced by a feeling of crushing defeat.¥

;五月の夕暮れ。神明神社の石段上。¥
`The May sun was setting now, illuminating the stone steps of the Kamiake Shrine.¥

;周囲の人間にこのことを話せば、
;恐らく俺は頭の中を疑われるに違いない。
;それほどに異常なはずだった。¥

;けれども、これが『溝口春樹と神明みのりの関係』であり、
;そして俺自身はこの関係を楽しいとさえ
;思っていたのだから、本当に異常なのかも知れない。¥
`And they would have been right, too.  This was the relationship that existed between us, physical violence and all.  And perhaps I really WAS insane -- because I did enjoy this so.¥

;他人以上、友人未満。¥
`More than strangers, less than friends,@
`each pursuing our own ends.¥

;お互いがお互いをそう思いながらも、
;心から楽しそうに話す。¥
`Of each other thinking such@
`yet how much fun to talk?  So much!¥

;異様なはずなのに、
;空は遠く、夕暮れは綺麗で、風は爽やかに、音は静かで、
;流れる空気はどこか優しかった。¥
`I should have felt it oh so strange@
`but sunset's glow was full of grace@
`as high May sky was out of range@
`I felt wind whisper on my face@
`for silence ever did not change@
`I gave myself to May's embrace.¥

`A million billion bodies were brutally crushing my body from every possible direction.  Compared against this human trash compactor, a rush hour commuter train was roomy.  Couldn't compare at all.¥

;力一杯かき分けようともがく。足が前の地面を踏めない。

;一回目は、撤退する重戦車と共に外まで追い出された。¥

;すっかり暇になってしまった俺は、

;ＢＧ：部屋

;五月二十九日、日曜日。午後２時。¥
`May twenty-ninth.  Sunday.  2 PM.¥

;>> ▽ 背景 ▽ 部屋 >>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
bg "May/BackGround/Room.jpg",3
;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>

;俺はぼんやりと椅子に座り、空の段ボールを眺めていた。¥
`I sat listlessly in a chair, staring at empty cardboard boxes.¥

;つい一ヶ月半前にお世話になったはずの段ボールは、
;今しがた引越し屋の兄ちゃんから受け取ったものだ。¥
`The irony of it was, I'd been unpacking boxes just like this in this very apartment not a month and a half ago, and now it was time to pack up again already.  I'd gone and gotten these from the moving company people earlier today.¥

;明日にはこの大きな段ボールの中に私物を入れ、
;明後日には引越し屋に預けなければならない。¥
`Tomorrow, I would put my belongings into these huge boxes.  The day after tomorrow was the movers' deadline.¥

;そして明々後日、
;３１日の新幹線で新居へ向かうという手筈になっている。¥
`And on the day after that -- May 31 -- I'd be getting on the bullet train to my new housing.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「………」¥
`"..."¥

;俺はただ、段ボールを睨むように見つめている。¥
`Except all that I was doing was staring at the cardboxes in useless anger.¥

;この街の六月に、俺はもういない。
;俺の六月は、新しい場所で仕事…というものになる。¥
`In June, I would vanish from these streets.  In June ... I'd be sitting behind a new desk in a new city.¥

;ここに永住する気は無かったが、
;こんなにも早く、そしてこんなにもあっさりと
;この街から離れるとは思わなかった。¥
`It wasn't that I wanted to stay here forever.  But on the other hand, I didn't want to leave so quickly.  And I didn't think that I could leave so easily -- or so simply.¥

;遠い場所への配属を聞かされて
;既に四日が経っているというのに、
;未だに気持ちの整理が出来てない。¥
`It had already been four days since it was made known to me that I had to move far away.  But all that time hadn't been enough for me to get my things -- or my thoughts -- in order.¥

;突然の衝撃に、
;未だに足がすくんでしまっている状態だった。
;思考は靄がかかったようにハッキリしない。¥
`It was one helluva shock.  Even now I was frozen by sheer fear of the prospect.  A fog wrapped around me; I could hardly think or see straight.¥

;先を見据えることが出来ず、
;足が止まったままに考え込んでいる。¥
`I couldn't look my future straight in the eye.  So instead I stood still, unable to move.  And thought on the situation.¥

;二ヶ月しかお世話にならなかったこの街に対し、
;『何かやり残したことはなかったか』と、考えている。¥
`I could only think to myself that now I'd be leaving this town -- this town that I'd only called home for two months -- without having changed a single thing in it or myself for the better.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「………」¥
`"..."¥

;俺はただ、段ボールを睨むように見つめている。
;生生しい、目の前に確かにある現実を見つめている。¥
`By 'think', I meant glaring at a pile of cardboard boxes.  I was staring at the suddenly very real, very harsh reality of the situation.¥

;四角のフォルムは無音で、それでいて大声で
;『もうここには戻ってこないんだよ』と訴えている。¥
`All those boxes were silent, of course.  But I could hear them accusing me loudly: "you're never coming back here".¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「………」¥
`"..."¥

;何か、やり残したことはなかったか。
;その思考だけが延々と頭の中を巡っている。¥
`I was leaving nothing of myself behind.  There would be no proof whatsoever that I had ever lived here.  That I had ever been.  I kept coming back to that one thought, again and again.¥

;もうここには帰ってこない。心残りは……。¥
`I was never coming back here.@/
`  And as for regrets ...¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「………」¥
`"..."¥
wait 500

;きっと、これは思考ではなく、覚悟なのだろう。¥
`... no.  Not regrets, not at all.  I wasn't as lost in self-pity as you might think.  No -- I was gathering my resolve.¥

;悩みながらも、既にやるべきことを考え終え、
;その選択を済まし、その状況を想定し、
;そして、結末に耐える覚悟をしているのだろう。¥
`Even as I worried like this, I'd already finished thinking about what I needed to do, justified the choices I was about to make to myself, run the possible scenarios through my head -- and, finally, steeled myself so I could see this through to the end.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「………」¥
`"..."¥

;やり残したことがある。ただ一つだけ、
;このまま引っ越してしまうと強く強く後悔する事項が、
;たった一つだけ。¥
`Because there WAS something I was leaving behind.  Just one.  A single thing that would eat me up inside if I left without doing anything about it.¥

;例えそれが痛みを伴おうとも、今やらねば、
;ずっと痛みを負い続けなければならない問題が
;一つだけある。¥
`Addressing the issue would hurt.  Hurt like hell, probably.  I knew that.  But I also knew that if I didn't do this right here and now, the hurt would never, ever go away.¥

;俺はそれを見つめている。
;無音で俺の背中を押すものを見つめている。¥
`And maybe for the first time in my life, I was looking straight at it ...@/
` straight at the thing that was weighing me down without a sound.¥

;【溝口 春樹】
`[ Haruki Mizoguchi ]
;「……よし」¥
`"... all right then."¥

;思考を終え、決意をした。覚悟は今終えた。
;あとは、行動だけ。¥
`No more thinking.  No more torment.  No more agonizing -- now was the time for resolution and action.  Now was the time to take the first step ...¥

;長々と座っていた椅子から降り、出かける支度を始めた。¥
`So I got up off the chair that I'd been so rooted on and made ready to leave.¥

;通勤に使っていたのとは逆に進む電車は、
;嘘のように席が空いていた。¥
`I boarded a train heading the opposite way on the same line I'd taken to work for this past month.  It was almost impossible to believe how many seats were empty.¥

;朝の日差しが車内に差し込み、
;芸能人のスキャンダル記事を載せた中吊り広告が
;せわしなく揺れている。¥
`The train interior was instead filled with fresh, morning sunlight.  Oh, and tabloids danging and swaying around, printed with news on actor scandals and the like.¥

;窓に映る景色は８０ｋｍのスピードで流れていく。
;左から右へ、何かを考える暇も思う暇も与えず、
;絶えず流れていく。¥
`We sped past the scenery at 80 kilometers per hour.  It really was all a blur.  No matter where I looked, I didn't have enough time to really think or consider any of it.  Everything was constantly, feverishly running past and behind me.¥

;座席が空いている中、
;ドアにもたれるようにして立っている俺は、
;若干不審に見られているかもしれなかった。¥
`And in the middle of this empty car, with all these empty seats surrounding me, I found myself standing and leaning against the door, watching everything without understanding anything.¥

;一秒一秒と刻々と時間は過ぎてゆく。
;あの街から離れていく。¥
`Time went on by.  Tick tock, one second, then another.  Marking out greater and greater distances from the town I'd called home for a month or two.¥

;【溝口 春樹】

;「………」¥

;慣れない操作でボタンを押し、アドレス帳を開くと、
;”か行”の所で『神明みのり』の表記が現れた。¥
`I pressed the button.  The process was unfamiliar.  I launched the address book.  "Minori Kamiake" came up under the K's.¥

;昨日今日と俺とみのりが歩いてきた道は
;風合瀬家のハイキングコースだったらしい。¥
`The "snow" area was practically in the Kasose family's BACK YARD.  We'd basically been going in one huge circle for all of yesterday and today.¥

;かなりの大回りをして
;あの場所に向かったということになったが、
;別段何を言うつもりも無く。¥
`SO IT WAS THE VERY, VERY LONG WAY AROUND TO THAT PLACE.  But they hadn't planned to tell me or anything.¥

;むしろ楽しかったくらいなのだから、
;この計らいに感謝していた。¥
`... then again, it had been more fun that way, and so I really did feel thankful for their arrangement.¥
delay 1500


;ライトバンの中には、風合瀬さんの笑い声が響いている。
;ハンドルが少しだけ急に回り、車体が揺れた。¥
`Mr. Kasose's laughter continued to fill the van.  He turned the steering wheel a bit sharply, making the vehicle shake.¥

;助手席のみのりは顔を真っ赤にして俯き、
;俺は頬を掻きながら山間から覗く空を見上げていた。¥
`In the passenger seat, Minori was red-faced, staring downwards.  Me, I scratched my cheeks and stared up at the mountain range, and the sky above that.¥

;昨日の夜についての質問は、
;風合瀬さん家に着くまでの間、機関銃の様に続いていた。¥
`For the entire time until we reached the Kasose house, Mr. Kasose relentlessly peppered us with questions, like some kind of human inquiry machine gun.¥
;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>

;がたんがたん、がたんがたん…。¥

;夏の日差しの差し込む電車の中。
;相変わらず乗客は自分達だけだった。¥
`Train wheels clicked and clacked.  We were inside a train car, its interior awash with summer sunlight.  Like the last time, we were the only passengers.¥

;車窓を流れる景色を見つめながら、
;肩にもたれかかって眠るみのりの体温を心地よく感じる。¥
`Minori's sleeping form was propped up against my shoulder, while I watched the scenery passing us by.  Her warmth felt comfortable, familiar.¥

;空には雄大な積雲が流れている。
;冷房が顔に涼しい冷気を送った。¥
`Magnificent cumulus clouds were flowing across the sky.  The air conditioning breathed cold currents again my face.¥
delay 1500

;目を閉じれば、記憶の中で、雪がまた降り始めた。¥
`When I closed my eyes, inside my memories, snow began to fall once again.¥

;じりじりと皮膚を焼くような熱気の下。
;青く広がる、夏空の下で。¥
`I was under a scorching hot, sunburn-causing, blue, wide, summer sky.¥

;八月の雪がしんしんと降り続く光景は、
;今も…きっとずっと、鮮明に有り続けている。¥
`That sight of silently falling snow in August was still ... and would surely, always be ... vivid and clear.  Forever.¥
delay 1500


;すぅすぅと幸せそうに寝息を立てるみのりの頭を
;優しく撫でる。¥
`Minori was breathing contentedly in her sleep.  I caressed her hair, gently.¥

;電車は大きく揺れて、
;みのりは『ううん…』と可愛らしい吐息を小さく漏らした。¥
`The train lurched, and Minori let out a sweet, faint sigh: "mmmm ..."¥

;>>> 背景 >>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>

;>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>

;その日も、夏の空はどこまでも青く、高くて、広かった。¥
`The summer sky was far and blue@
`Now and ever ringing true¥

;太陽から降り注ぐ日光は熱く、強く、輝いていた。¥
`The tender rays of daylight's star@
`Came shining strong from space afar¥

;二人を乗せた電車は
;高温の路面を滑るようにして走っていく。¥
`The two of us inside this train@
`Were gliding toward future's refrain¥

;その先には、きっと一週間前と変わらない日常と、
;あの場所が待っている。¥
`And just ahead were days unchanged@
`Waiting for us to come once more@
`The same routine, nothing exchanged@
`But now for us what was in store?¥
